    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({

        scope : 'name email',

<div id="descriptionContainer">
  
      <div id="description" class="readable stacked" style="right:0">
        
<span id="freeTextContainer17022910779952328767">The mind guides our footsteps as we progress along the pathway of life.<br/><br/>Purity of mind leads inevitably to purity of life, to the precious love and understanding that should control our everyday acts and attitudes towards friends and foes.<br/><br/>But where must one look for guidance? How does one achieve purity of mind that alone brings happiness and confidence?<br/><br/>The author offers hi</span>
  <span id="freeText17022910779952328767" style="display:none">The mind guides our footsteps as we progress along the pathway of life.<br /><br />Purity of mind leads inevitably to purity of life, to the precious love and understanding that should control our everyday acts and attitudes towards friends and foes.<br /><br />But where must one look for guidance? How does one achieve purity of mind that alone brings happiness and confidence?<br /><br />The author offers his clear answers in this book <i>As A Man Thinketh</i>. His words have helped millions for more than a century--and they continue to point the true way to a better life for a troubled humanity.<br /><br />"Out of a clean heart comes a clean life and a clean body," James Allen writes. "Out of a defiled mind proceeds a defiled life and a corrupt body."<br /><br />Too many mortals strive to improve only their wordly position--and too few seek spiritual betterment. Such is the problem James Allen faced in his own time. The ideas he found in his inner-most heart after great searching guided him as they will guide you.</span>
  <a data-text-id="17022910779952328767" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

Popular Answered Questions

<div class='communityQuestionAndAnswer'>
<div class='communityQuestion'>
<div class='questionText'>
<a href="/questions/499536-what-does-author-mean-by---no-such">What does author mean by - No such conditions can exist as descending into vice and its attendant sufferings apart from vicious inclinations, or ascending into virtue and its pure happiness without the continued cultivation of virtuous aspirations; in the section EFFECT OF THOUGHT ON CIRCUMSTANCES.?</a>
</div>
<div class='communityQAFooter questionFooter'>
<ul class='questionFooterActions'>
<li class='footerItem like'>
<span class='likeItContainer' id='like_container_community_question_499536'><a id="like_count_community_question_499536" rel="nofollow" href="/rating/voters/499536?resource_type=CommunityQuestion"><span class="likesCount">4 likes</span></a>&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;<a rel="nofollow" class="jsLike like_it" href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/new?remember=true&amp;return_url=%2Fbook%2Fshow%2F81959.As_a_Man_Thinketh">like</a></span>

</li>
<li class='footerItem communityQuestionTimestamp'>
<a href="/questions/499536-what-does-author-mean-by---no-such">5 years ago</a>
</li>
<li class='footerItem communityQuestionPermalink'>
<a href="/questions/499536-what-does-author-mean-by---no-such">See all 3 answers</a>
</li>
</ul>
</div>

</div>
<div class='allCommunityAnswers'>
<div class='communityAnswer'>
<div class='communityAnswerBody'>
<div class='answererUserIcon'>
<a class="leftAlignedImage userPhoto" href="/user/show/47967582-kevin-zielinski"><img alt="" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/users/1526858996i/47967582._UY100_CR0,0,100,100_.jpg" /></a>
</div>
<div class='communityAnswerTextContainer'>
<span class='communityAnswererName'>
<a href="/user/show/47967582-kevin-zielinski">Kevin Zielinski</a>
</span>
<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">He's further illustrating the main idea of this chapter and the grand theme woven throughout the book: that is, "circumstances grow out of thought." H<a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">He's further illustrating the main idea of this chapter and the grand theme woven throughout the book: that is, "circumstances grow out of thought." His point being that our outward circumstances (i.e. drunkenness or some other vice) occur in direct proportion to our inward thoughts (i.e. vicious inclinations). The same law is true for the opposite of vice (i.e. virtuous behavior), which springs forth in direct proportion to inward virtuous aspirations. <br />Simply put, we cannot fake outwardly what we think inwardly for very long. Thoughts--whether they be positive or negative--manifest physically if given enough time. Hence, "The human mind may be liked to a garden which may be intelligently cultivated or allowed to run wild," and "Thoughts and character are one, and as character can manifest and discover itself only through environment and circumstance, the outer conditions of our life will always be found to be harmoniously related to our inner state."<br /><br />I always liken the idea to this metaphor: When my mind and thoughts are a mess, so too is my room or house or outside environment also messy. What's on the outside reflects what's on the inside. <a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>
</span>
</div>
</div>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/483217544" />
    <a title="Sanjay Gautam" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/10179929-sanjay-gautam"><img alt="Sanjay Gautam" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1427923732p2/10179929.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/483217544?book_show_action=true">Dec 22, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sanjay Gautam" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sanjay Gautam" href="/user/show/10179929-sanjay-gautam">Sanjay Gautam</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9789380816470" href="/book/show/25104105-as-a-man-thinketh">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer483217544" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5528836909447587608"><br/><i>"As a man thinketh in his heart, so is he."</i><br/><br/>Thought is the seed for action. If you control the cause- you can control the effect. The main message of this succinct, yet powerful, book is: <i>the quality of your thoughts determine your quality of life.</i> If your thoughts are pure and good, your life will also be good; and vice versa.<br/><br/><br/><i>"Man's mind may be likened to a garden, which may be intelligently cultivated or allowed to run wild; but whether cultivated or neglected, it must, and will, bring forth. I</i></span>
  <span id="freeText5528836909447587608" style="display:none"><br /><i>"As a man thinketh in his heart, so is he."</i><br /><br />Thought is the seed for action. If you control the cause- you can control the effect. The main message of this succinct, yet powerful, book is: <i>the quality of your thoughts determine your quality of life.</i> If your thoughts are pure and good, your life will also be good; and vice versa.<br /><br /><br /><i>"Man's mind may be likened to a garden, which may be intelligently cultivated or allowed to run wild; but whether cultivated or neglected, it must, and will, bring forth. If no useful seeds are put into it, then an abundance of useless weed-seeds will fall therein, and will produce their kind."</i><br /><br />The author maintains: The man is the master of thought, the moulder of character, and the maker and shaper of condition, environment, and destiny. He compares the human mind with a garden and the man with a gardener. Just like a gardener removes the weeds from his garden so must we discard the impure and useless thoughts from our mind and must concentrate on cultivating the useful and pure thoughts. By the right choice and true application of thoughts, man ascends towards perfection.<br /><br />On a different note: I found this book to be the source of books rooted in 'law of attraction' approaches. The books such as: Magic of Believing, The Secret, etc. - bear a striking resemblance with this book. Needless to say this book has been very influential since its publication. <br /><br /><br /><br />My actual rating: 3.5/5.0<br /><br />Recommended! <br /><br /><br /></span>

  <span id="freeText7172600629001610216" style="display:none">I read this book yesterday. I really enjoyed it and have set some new personal development goals in line with the book's concepts. This is a book I will reread throughout my life.<br /><br />I do disagree with one point. James Allen said that bad thoughts lead to sickness and disease, which is the part I agree with. He also said the reverse is true, bad health is a result of bad thoughts, which I do not agree. I don't believe that all sickness and disease is a result of bad thoughts or sin. I believe that we have mortal bodies that are prone to sickness and degeneration. Yes, bad thoughts do corrupt the body and can lead to bad health, but the reverse is not always true. When it rains the sidewalk gets wet, but just because the sidewalk is wet, doesn't mean it has rained.<br /></span>

<div id="review_616363390" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/616363390" />
    <a title="Tom Lombardo" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/16991830-tom-lombardo"><img alt="Tom Lombardo" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1576208832p2/16991830.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/616363390?book_show_action=true">May 15, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Tom Lombardo" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Tom Lombardo" href="/user/show/16991830-tom-lombardo">Tom Lombardo</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="ebook 9781418551223" href="/book/show/16602799-as-a-man-thinketh">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16991830-tom-lombardo?shelf=inspirational">inspirational</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer616363390" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7449572267638027561">In 2003, a number of leading self-help authors were asked to list the works that were, to them, most inspirational. The book mentioned most often was James Allen's <em>As a Man Thinketh</em>.<br/><br/>Despite the fact that his books have been inspirational for generations, very little is known about the man himself. He was born in Leicester, England. When he was fifteen his father was brutally murdered by a robber, forcing Allen out of school and into the workforce. He eventually worked his way up to the position </span>
  <span id="freeText7449572267638027561" style="display:none">In 2003, a number of leading self-help authors were asked to list the works that were, to them, most inspirational. The book mentioned most often was James Allen's <em>As a Man Thinketh</em>.<br /><br />Despite the fact that his books have been inspirational for generations, very little is known about the man himself. He was born in Leicester, England. When he was fifteen his father was brutally murdered by a robber, forcing Allen out of school and into the workforce. He eventually worked his way up to the position of executive secretary for a high ranking officer of an English corporation.<br /><br />Then, at the age of 38, he retired with his wife to a small cottage in Ilfracombe, a tiny town on the northernmost coast of England. In 1902 <em>As a Man Thinketh</em> was published - about the same time Allen made this move. He and his wife intentionally pursued a simple life of gardening and contemplation. In the next ten years, Allen wrote more than twenty more books, and then he suddenly died at the age of 48, in 1912.<br /><br />This book is barely 7,800 words long - about thirty pages of a typically printed paperback. And yet it rewards every single reading, no matter how many times you return to it. Each sentence is a pearl of truth and wisdom; each word carries as much meaning as a single word possibly can. If you read it once and underline every statement that strikes you as profoundly true, and then read it again, still underlining, and then again, you will underline the entire book.<br /><br />As with all books like this, the author is careful to acknowledge that everything he is about to say has been said many times before. On the first page he opens with a quote from the <em>The Dhammapada: The Sayings of the Buddha</em>, which is based upon an oral tradition that may be 10,000 years old.<br /><br />The ancient "wisdom" Allen summarizes for us is not really "wisdom" at all. <em>It is fact;</em> accepting it as such can completely rejuvenate your life. The exact same insights are illuminatingly presented Napoleon Hill's classic, <em>Think and Grow Rich</em>.<br /><br />James Allen's words still resonate today because he speaks of the very nature of consciousness. Since our consciousness is entirely under our control -- which Viktor Frankl shows us is the case even in the most horrific of conditions in his heartrending classic <em>Man's Search for Meaning</em> -- then our ultimate responsibility is for us to use our consciousness in the proper way. The essential idea that we can control consciousness is hotly debated by theologians, but if we accept for the moment that we can control our thoughts, the next obvious question is what we ought to do with them. Here is one of Allen's most succinct instructions:<br /><br /><blockquote>A man's mind may be likened to a garden, which may be intelligently cultivated or allowed to run wild; but whether cultivated or neglected, it must, and will, bring forth. If no useful seeds are put into it, then an abundance of useless weed-seeds will fall therein, and will continue to produce their kind.<br /><br />Just as a gardener cultivates his plot, keeping it free from weeds, and growing the flowers and fruits which he requires, so may a man tend the garden of his mind, weeding out all the wrong, useless, and impure thoughts, and cultivating toward perfection the flowers and fruits of right, useful, and pure thoughts. By pursuing this process, a man sooner or later discovers that he is the master-gardener of his soul, the director of his life. He also reveals, within himself, the laws of thought, and understands, with ever-increasing accuracy, how the thought-forces and mind-elements operate in the shaping of his character, circumstances, and destiny.<br /><br />Thought and character are one, and as character can only manifest and discover itself through environment and circumstance, the outer conditions of a person's life will always be found to be harmoniously related to his inner state. This does not mean that a man's circumstances at any given time are an indication of his entire character, but that those circumstances are so intimately connected with some vital thought-element within himself that, for the time being, they are indispensable to his development.<br /><br />Every man is where he is by the law of his being; the thoughts which he has built into his character have brought him there, and in the arrangement of his life there is no element of chance, but all is the result of a law which cannot err. This is just as true of those who feel "out of harmony" with their surroundings as of those who are contented with them.<br /><br />As a progressive and evolving being, man is where he is that he may learn that he may grow; and as he learns the spiritual lesson which any circumstance contains for him, it passes away and gives place to other circumstances.<br /><br />Man is buffeted by circumstances so long as he believes himself to be the creature of outside conditions, but when he realizes that he is a creative power, and that he may command the hidden soil and seeds of his being out of which circumstances grow, he then becomes the rightful master of himself.<br /><br />That circumstances grow out of thought every man knows who has for any length of time practiced self-control and self-purification, for he will have noticed that the alteration in his circumstances has been in exact ratio with his altered mental condition. So true is this that when a man earnestly applies himself to remedy the defects in his character, and makes swift and marked progress, he passes rapidly through a succession of vicissitudes.<br /><br />The soul attracts that which it secretly harbors; that which it loves, and also that which it fears; it reaches the height of its cherished aspirations; it falls to the level of its unchastened desires; and circumstances are the means by which the soul receives its own.<br /><br />Every thought-seed sown or allowed to fall into the mind, and to take root there, produces its own, blossoming sooner or later into act, and bearing its own fruitage of opportunity and circumstances. Good thoughts bear good fruit, bad thoughts bad fruit.<br /><br />The outer world of circumstance shapes itself to the inner world of thought, and both pleasant and unpleasant external conditions are factors which make for the ultimate good of the individual. As the reaper of his own harvest, man learns both by suffering and bliss.<br /><br />Following the inmost desires, aspirations, thoughts, by which he allows himself to be dominated (pursuing the will-o'-the-wisps of impure imagining or steadfastly walking the highway of strong and high endeavor), a man at last arrives at their fruition and fulfillment in the outer condition of his life.</blockquote><br /><br />Allen also addresses the anxiety that you might feel the moment you accept this wisdom as truth. You might worry that your negative thoughts are going to manifest themselves around you. You may also worry that you can't control your mind - that it presents "impure imagining" to you whether you want it to or not.<br /><br />This is the human condition; you are not alone. The method for gaining control of your "innermost desires, aspirations, [and] thoughts" is to work at it continuously. Become aware of your mind, and simply do not berate yourself. Learn how to let negativity flow into the past, and how to begin again from the moment. When you scold yourself for having a negative thought, let that, too, flow into the past, and begin again. Focus on what you want, or if you don't know what you want, focus on thoughts that will lead you to know what you want. There is no other way.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="7449572267638027561" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_2771308738" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2771308738" />
    <a title="Apoorva" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/25605420-apoorva"><img alt="Apoorva" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1597844654p2/25605420.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2771308738?book_show_action=true">Apr 01, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Apoorva" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Apoorva" href="/user/show/25605420-apoorva">Apoorva</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/32948046-as-a-man-thinketh">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25605420-apoorva?shelf=non-fiction">non-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25605420-apoorva?shelf=personal-development">personal-development</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25605420-apoorva?shelf=philosophy-religion">philosophy-religion</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2771308738" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6306659570698696355"><b>
  <i>Mind is the Master power that moulds and makes,<br/>And Man is Mind, and evermore he takes<br/>The tool of Thought, and, shaping what he wills,<br/>Brings forth a thousand joys, a thousand ills:—<br/>He thinks in secret, and it comes to pass:<br/>Environment is but his looking-glass.</i>
</b><br/><br/>This is a short and inspiring philosophical book with its title being influenced by a verse in the Bible. The author also makes references to Jesus, Krishna, and Buddha while explaining his ideas. The central theme of the book is that a </span>
  <span id="freeText6306659570698696355" style="display:none"><b>
  <i>Mind is the Master power that moulds and makes,<br />And Man is Mind, and evermore he takes<br />The tool of Thought, and, shaping what he wills,<br />Brings forth a thousand joys, a thousand ills:—<br />He thinks in secret, and it comes to pass:<br />Environment is but his looking-glass.</i>
</b><br /><br />This is a short and inspiring philosophical book with its title being influenced by a verse in the Bible. The author also makes references to Jesus, Krishna, and Buddha while explaining his ideas. The central theme of the book is that a man is shaped by the thoughts he harbors whether consciously or subconsciously. Good and positive thoughts will attract joy and peace while negative thoughts will attract misery and despair. If he finds himself in an unfortunate situation that is out of his control, he needs to accept the fact that nothing lasts forever. <br /><br />He can choose to find the good things from an unpleasant experience while from the bad things, he can learn important lessons. He can let the failure and pain guide and motivate him to improve himself and his life to earn the success he rightfully deserves. This will cause him to take ownership of his life and not blame other people for everything that is wrong in his life.<br /> <br />All a person needs to do is alter the way he perceives a situation. If you see the world as your ally, you’ll find that the world is a beautiful thing that wants you to succeed and it’ll present endless people and opportunities to achieve those goals and if you believe that the world is conspiring against you, you’ll find yourself at war with the enemy you can’t conquer and live with perpetual hell of your own making. Our thoughts will manifest into his habits and the habits will shape our circumstances because mind and body are intimately connected.<br /><br />If you want to live a successful life, you need to have a passion or a vision of an ideal life. If you have a picture of what an ideal life looks like to you, you’re going to work really hard to achieve that and the unfavorable circumstance you’re in right now will seem like a temporary state that you’ll eventually get out of. Using the basic rule of cause and effect, instead of worrying about things you can’t control, you can focus on giving the best from your side. If that doesn’t work, you’ll need to learn to find better and efficient ways and try again. <br /><br />A calm person draws strength from within so the external circumstances don’t faze him. What you get is what you deserve in life and if you don’t have it then you need to work for it and earn it. It’s mostly how to use the law of attraction to your maximum benefit. The author also talks about the benefits of meditation in your daily life and interesting discussion about the cause of suffering and how to reach a state of enlightenment.<br /><br />All in all, a nice short read.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="6306659570698696355" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_126051245" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/126051245" />
    <a title="Jesse Field" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3633038-jesse-field"><img alt="Jesse Field" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1273174024p2/3633038.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/126051245?book_show_action=true">Oct 13, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jesse Field" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jesse Field" href="/user/show/3633038-jesse-field">Jesse Field</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer126051245" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13932444295657610783">"Thought allied fearlessly to purpose becomes creative force." This is the basic idea behind all of James Allen's sugary half-truths. When I found an audio file with this text pre-packaged into my new learnoutloud.com cart, read by "Brian Johnson, Philosopher and CEO of Zaadz.com," I was briefly intrigued. <br/><br/>Then as I listened a bit more, I thought it was some kind of joke or parody -- surely in just a moment Brian, "Philosopher," will put on a more genuine, critical voice. Surely he would tell us</span>
  <span id="freeText13932444295657610783" style="display:none">"Thought allied fearlessly to purpose becomes creative force." This is the basic idea behind all of James Allen's sugary half-truths. When I found an audio file with this text pre-packaged into my new learnoutloud.com cart, read by "Brian Johnson, Philosopher and CEO of Zaadz.com," I was briefly intrigued. <br /><br />Then as I listened a bit more, I thought it was some kind of joke or parody -- surely in just a moment Brian, "Philosopher," will put on a more genuine, critical voice. Surely he would tell us that of course you can't change your circumstances with your thoughts. That's not philosophy, but magical thinking. Surely he would remind us, as <a href="http://www.guardian.co.uk/books/2010/jan/10/smile-or-die-barbara-ehrenreich" rel="nofollow noopener">Barbara Erhenreich</a> has tried to do, that perfectly virtuous people fail and suffer everyday. And that perfect scoundrals, animalistic beasts, succeed and prosper all the time. (For some reason I think of Adam Sandler. I believe he once commented with pride that he did not finish high school.) <br /><br />Surely people all know, in this day and age, that "serenity" is not a viable goal in life? That the best we can do is meet the challenges as they come, acknowledge that life is always a struggle, and find reasons to continue the struggle? <br /><br />Surely people don't fall for this dully polished hogwash, already dreadfully unoriginal by 1903? Doesn't the pompousness, the selfishness, the sheer vacuity of Allen's thinking show through?<br /><br />Sadly, there truly is no end to how gullible readers can be. I suppose when you combine basic ignorance with the anxiety and ambivalence we all feel these days (trust me I feel it too) then the result is that a large part of the population will continue to purchase the age-old idea that "right thoughts" will change the world. That's why <a href="http://www.philosophersnotes.com/brianjohnson" rel="nofollow noopener">Brian Johnson</a> can live the glamorous, self-oriented life of a "CEO." That's why Allen's 1903 text is plastered all over the internet, from Wikipedia to Project Gutenberg and so on and so forth. I've hit on yet another node of the most compelling <b>fantasy</b> that exists in this market-and-work oriented world. <br /><br />"There's a sucker born every minute." - P.T. Barnum (died 1891)</span>
  <a data-text-id="13932444295657610783" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_26178774" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/26178774" />
    <a title="Annalisa" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/542037-annalisa"><img alt="Annalisa" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1226336540p2/542037.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/26178774?book_show_action=true">Jul 02, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Annalisa" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Annalisa" href="/user/show/542037-annalisa">Annalisa</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780760733936" href="/book/show/81962.As_a_Man_Thinketh">review of another edition</a>


          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Annalisa by: </span>
      Crystalyn
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/542037-annalisa?shelf=non-fiction">non-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/542037-annalisa?shelf=religion-philosophy">religion-philosophy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer26178774" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7592534234097181071">A small collection of thoughts on how powerful our minds truly are, this is book you'll want to turn to again and again because though it's short, it's deep with meaning. There is no fluff to distract our brains from epiphany to epiphany. Some of my favorite quotes:<br/>Thought and character are one. <br/>The dreamers are the saviors of the world. <br/>In all human affairs there are efforts, and there are results, and the strength of the effort is the measure of the result. Chance is not. <br/>A man is literally wh</span>
  <span id="freeText7592534234097181071" style="display:none">A small collection of thoughts on how powerful our minds truly are, this is book you'll want to turn to again and again because though it's short, it's deep with meaning. There is no fluff to distract our brains from epiphany to epiphany. Some of my favorite quotes:<br />Thought and character are one. <br />The dreamers are the saviors of the world. <br />In all human affairs there are efforts, and there are results, and the strength of the effort is the measure of the result. Chance is not. <br />A man is literally what he thinks, his character being the complete sum of all his thoughts.<br />Act is the blossom of thought, and joy and suffering are its fruits. <br />Circumstance does not make the man; it reveals him to himself. <br />Men do not attract that which they want, but that which they are. <br />Indigence and indulgence are the two extremes of wretchedness.<br />He who has conquered doubt and fear has conquered failure. <br />Thought allied fearlessly to purpose becomes creative force. <br />They who have no central purpose in their life fall an easy prey to petty worries, fears, troubles, and self-pityings. <br />Victories attained by right thought can only be maintained by watchfulness. <br />Men imagine that thought can be kept secret, but it cannot; it rapidly crystallizes into habit, and habit solidifies into circumstance. <br />There is no physician like cheerful thought for dissipating the ills of the body; there is no comforter to compare with good will for dispersing the shadows of grief and sorrow. <br />A man cannot directly choose his circumstances, but he can choose his thoughts, and so indirectly, yet surely, shape is circumstances. <br /><br />Why the four stars? There are a few statements that did not quite win me over. Such as: <br />Wrinkles are not manifestations of age but poor character, and health issues are manifestations of a poor mind. I'm not denying that thought affects health, but it is not the only cursor for poor health.<br />Suffering is always the effect of wrong thought in some direction. Only most of the time. Sometimes we suffer most in our vulnerability to those we love when they do wrong or hurt us or suffer themselves. This godly sorrow may not be what he means by suffering, but I also can't imagine suffering at the unforseen death of a loved one to be suffering of our own making, unless you are considering it to be a challenge in life you chose to encounter. <br />Calmness is a virtue every human should aspire. While steady demeanor is a worthy goal, there is much to be said for enthusiasm, emotion, and variety in personalities. While tempers and impatience are not good qualities, neither is a lack of emotion, and there is nothing wrong with a happy animated person, a person I would never describe as calm. Calm is a great quality, but it's not the all-inclusive. If he had said peace, I would understand. </span>
  <a data-text-id="7592534234097181071" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer83810591" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14388759143981647967">I found this in one of my apartments on my religious mission, and it looks like it used to be required reading. I read it then and thought it was decent. I read it recently and thought it was pretty poor. It felt a little bit too much like "The Secret" ... just think about something and you'll get it. If you think good thoughts you'll have a good happy life and vice versa. If only those people suffering genocide in Darfur could think better thoughts...<br/><br/>To be fair, I do agree to an extent and know</span>
  <span id="freeText14388759143981647967" style="display:none">I found this in one of my apartments on my religious mission, and it looks like it used to be required reading. I read it then and thought it was decent. I read it recently and thought it was pretty poor. It felt a little bit too much like "The Secret" ... just think about something and you'll get it. If you think good thoughts you'll have a good happy life and vice versa. If only those people suffering genocide in Darfur could think better thoughts...<br /><br />To be fair, I do agree to an extent and know that focusing your energy and thoughts on something will help you achieve said goal, or help you to be a particular way. And we all know the power of positive thinking. I guess I can agree on some of Allen's premises here, but I feel like he takes it too far, and man does he beat a dead horse. This book just repeats itself over and over and gets a bit tiresome, especially for something so short.</span>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">The Secret fans</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5312798-gergana?shelf=non-fiction">non-fiction</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1183988726" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1956695606147373881">I can hardly believe that this book was published in 1902! <br/><br/>If you know about the "Law of Attraction" it's very likely you found out about it from a movie called <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/52529.The_Secret__The_Secret___1_' title='The Secret (The Secret, #1) by Rhonda Byrne' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Secret</a> that came out in 2006 - a 100 years later! A part of the human population was blown away by it (me included), other parts were either amused, disturbed, hated it or found it hard to care.<br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1437739680i/15623907.jpg' width='300' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><b>Now, this <s>review</s> <s>contemplation</s> <s>rant</s> <i>WHATEVER</i> will be weird, especially if you don't believe in the Law of Attraction. It's very likely you'll</b></span>
  <span id="freeText1956695606147373881" style="display:none">I can hardly believe that this book was published in 1902! <br><br>If you know about the "Law of Attraction" it's very likely you found out about it from a movie called <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/52529.The_Secret__The_Secret___1_" title="The Secret (The Secret, #1) by Rhonda Byrne" rel="nofollow noopener">The Secret</a> that came out in 2006 - a 100 years later! A part of the human population was blown away by it (me included), other parts were either amused, disturbed, hated it or found it hard to care.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1437739680i/15623907.jpg" width="300" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>Now, this <s>review</s> <s>contemplation</s> <s>rant</s> <i>WHATEVER</i> will be weird, especially if you don't believe in the Law of Attraction. It's very likely you'll end up thinking I need some serious help. XD </b> Which is fine, you don't know where I live anyways.<br><br>Before I say anything else, I have to admit that although I practice the Law (I freak out every time it works) and I agree with the majority of the teachings (e.g. if you have problems in life they are your own doing, stop complaining, see the bright side/opportunity, etc.) <b>I am rather concerned with the general obsession for owning stuff and believing that having something that you currently lack will bring you happiness. </b> So in this new "happiness movement" people often get encouraged to <b>desire</b> stuff. (Or at least imagine we already have them). Why? Cause you <b>HAVE TO!</b> We all know that owning the newest piece of technology will make us happier. Just look at all those happy faces in the smartphone TV ads. Or how happy physically fit and attractive people look on the Posters. They definitely get to pick the best husbands/wives. Look at the rich people on the news! I bet they've never had health/family/mental problems - owning a Rolls Royce guarantees perfect life!<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1437739680i/15623908._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>We are almost being conditioned to <b>desire</b>, to think happy thoughts all the time, to wish for better jobs, more money, a truer love, bigger home, etc. And we often end up neglecting what we currently posses. In fact, the more we believe that thoughts can attract something better, the more we might end up hating the situation we are currently in. The main problem is.... why do we desire it in the first place? <b>Who</b> taught us to want it? Will it really make us happier? And when do we put a stop to it? What do we do if we become addicted to "desiring"? What if we are never satisfied?<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1437739681i/15623909.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>For example - you can desire for the perfect mate (boyfriend/girlfriend), but if the mate does something "wrong" or disagrees with you, would you wish for a new/better one right away? If it's easy and quick? Why waste your time and energy dealing with a problem, learning tolerance or practicing forgiveness, when all you have to do is just move on the next option?<br><br>I guess, what I'm trying to say is- don't take this book (and The Secret) way too seriously. Life is not meant to be spent solely on chasing after dreams or wishing for a better future. Sometimes, problems happen for a reason and sometimes misfortune is what makes us better, more human. <br><br><b>In my experience, the Law worked in two cases:</b><br>1. When my mind is cleared (after experiencing some dramatic phase of my life) and I am super focused on what I want for a couple of days, then I stop thinking about it completely. It usually takes 4-5 days for things/people to "manifest" (and that still scares the shit out of me).<br>2. When I end up being happy with what I have, practice mindfulness and just feel super relaxed. This takes longer, because I don't really desire anything at this stage, but if I remember to wish for something I just do it for a few minutes and then go back to being "present".<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1437740636i/15624005.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><s>Un</s>Fortunately, I'm too busy with life to really spend too much time contemplating the "wrongness" of my current situation.<br><br>Don't wish for something when you are feeling depressed for not having it. Not having lots of money/perfect partner/great carrier according to the society's standards is not "wrong", unless you believe it.<br><br>If you are stuck and you find it hard to "manifest", try reading the teachings of Buddha, Tao or Toltec Philosophy to balance the "ego".<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1437740376i/15623961.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>The Secret is better written, better explained, more practical and more relevant, but I would still recommend As a Man Thinketh for everyone who is curious. It's a revolutionary (but not very well-known) piece of work that has also inspired Napoleon Hill to write <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/1005.Think_and_Grow_Rich" title="Think and Grow Rich by Napoleon Hill" rel="nofollow noopener">Think and Grow Rich</a>. Anyways, if you want to start from somewhere, start with <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/52529.The_Secret__The_Secret___1_" title="The Secret (The Secret, #1) by Rhonda Byrne" rel="nofollow noopener">The Secret</a> and try to keep reading/watching the DVD. The first half hour is damn right freaky and feels like you are watching some weird religious propaganda if you're new to it. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1437740376i/15623962._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></span>
  <a data-text-id="1956695606147373881" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer17870688421225227380"><b>دوستان عزیز این کتاب بی نظیر رو که الهام بخش آدمهای بسیار بزرگی مثل آنتونی رابینز، جیم ران و ... هست رو حتما نگاهی بهش داشته باشید. بعد از خوندن تنها یک صفحه متوجه عمق و زیبایی مطالبش می شید.</b><br/><b>This wonderful book is one the most exquisite, delicate, books I've ever read.</b> Statements being uttered in the book carry a heavy deal of wisdom while gently they touch your soul. Here are some of them:<br/><br/>-The outer conditions of a person's life will always be found to be harmoniously related to his inner state</span>
  <span id="freeText17870688421225227380" style="display:none"><b>دوستان عزیز این کتاب بی نظیر رو که الهام بخش آدمهای بسیار بزرگی مثل آنتونی رابینز، جیم ران و ... هست رو حتما نگاهی بهش داشته باشید. بعد از خوندن تنها یک صفحه متوجه عمق و زیبایی مطالبش می شید.</b><br /><b>This wonderful book is one the most exquisite, delicate, books I've ever read.</b> Statements being uttered in the book carry a heavy deal of wisdom while gently they touch your soul. Here are some of them:<br /><br />-The outer conditions of a person's life will always be found to be harmoniously related to his inner state.<br />-Men do not attract that which they want, but that which they are. <br />-Not what he wished and prays for does a man get, but what he justly earns. His wishes and prayers are only gratified and answered when they <b>harmonize with his <u>thoughts</u> and <u>actions</u></b>.<br />-A man cannot directly choose his circumstances, but he can choose his thoughts, and so indirectly, yet surely, shape hist circumstances.<br />-When a man makes his thoughts pure, he no longer desires impure food.<br />-Clean thoughts make clean habits. <br />-The so-called saint who does not wash his body is not a saint.<br />-Until thought is linked with purpose there is no intelligent accomplishment.<br />-One man is an oppressor because many are slaves, let us despise the slaves...<br />-You will become as small as your controlling desire, as great as your dominant aspiration.</span>

  <div class="friendReviews elementListBrown" >
    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_2267755023" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2267755023" />
    <a title="Fuzaila" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/55299343-fuzaila"><img alt="Fuzaila" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1532881347p2/55299343.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2267755023?book_show_action=true">Jan 26, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Fuzaila" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Fuzaila" href="/user/show/55299343-fuzaila">Fuzaila</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Fuzaila by: </span>
      Sharjeel
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/55299343-fuzaila?shelf=classics">classics</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/55299343-fuzaila?shelf=non-fiction">non-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/55299343-fuzaila?shelf=could-have-been-better">could-have-been-better</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2267755023" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8799674894196743018"><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>"As a man thinketh in his heart so is he"</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br/>^ That one sentence sums up the whole idea of this book, or rather, an essay.<br/><br/>In As a Man Thinketh, James Allen strongly professes the concept that a man is only as good as his thoughts. While in a sense, it may be true, you could also argue against it. It has a lot of possibilities for an amusing, thought-provoking debate. <br/>Look at this – <br/><br/>	●<blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“A man does not come to the almshouse or the jail by the tyranny of fate or circumstance, but by </i></b></blockquote></span>
  <span id="freeText8799674894196743018" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>"As a man thinketh in his heart so is he"</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br />^ That one sentence sums up the whole idea of this book, or rather, an essay.<br /><br />In As a Man Thinketh, James Allen strongly professes the concept that a man is only as good as his thoughts. While in a sense, it may be true, you could also argue against it. It has a lot of possibilities for an amusing, thought-provoking debate. <br />Look at this – <br /><br />	●<blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“A man does not come to the almshouse or the jail by the tyranny of fate or circumstance, but by the pathway of groveling thoughts and base desires. Nor does a pure-minded man fall suddenly into crime by stress of any mere external force; the criminal thought had long been secretly fostered in the heart, and the hour of opportunity revealed its gathered power.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br /><br />Unsurprisingly, I was reminded of Jean Val Jean while reading this sentence. Not surprised if you did too. We all have loved that character, who, out of sheer desperation to feed his family, stole a piece of bread and ended up in prison. Theft is a crime, no matter what they say, but feeding your family is not. Bringing up this fictional scenario to point out that Allen is wrong, is not my intention though. I’d rather you think of all the poor people there, who were tried and tested in court, many sentenced to death, because they did something similar, or worse. Does that justification make them any less guilty? No. But does that knowledge lessen your hatred for the said accused? Admit it, it did. <br /><br />	●<blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>"Circumstance does not make the man; it reveals him to himself”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br /><br />So what does that say about the person’s thoughts? Had he always harbored ill thoughts, thought of stealing, killing, murdering? He might have. Could he have avoided those thoughts if he willed himself hard enough? The answer is <b>NO</b>. Point blank. <br /><br />However hard we try, a controlled mind always slips, always blends in with its surroundings, because just like a coin with two sides, a mind is composed of bad thoughts as much as the good ones. We may think bad stuff, and will ourselves not to do it. But when we actually do something bad, it is NOT BECAUSE WE HAD THOUGHT OF IT ONCE BEFORE. Of course, it is just what I feel to be true, you may have arguments that I may counter-argue. Still, <b>I STRONGLY BELIEVE THAT THE COMPLETE CONTROL OF ONES’ MIND BY ONES’ SELF, IS NOT POSSIBLE.</b><br /><br />	●<blockquote>
  <b>
    <i> "A man cannot directly choose his circumstances, but he can choose his thoughts, and so indirectly, yet surely, shape his circumstances”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br /><br />That, my friends, I whole-heartedly disagree with. <b>You can choose to be good or bad, but you definitely cannot choose to <i>think</i> good thoughts or bad thoughts.</b> Duh. Try it for yourself if you don’t believe me.<br /><br />	●<blockquote>
  <i> “Change of diet will not help a man who will not change his thoughts. When a man makes his thoughts pure, he no longer desires impure food.”</i>
</blockquote><br />I mean, seriously? What someone eats is his own business, you idiot. Even if you eat a snake, or a man for that matter, your body will adjust unless there are other ways for survival. Alright?<br /><br />	●<blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>"The will to do springs from the knowledge that we can do. Doubt and fear are the great enemies of knowledge, and he who encourages them, who does not slay them, thwarts himself at every step."</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br /><br />However impressive the above sentence might be, I can’t think of confining the whole of human behavioral pattern and thoughts to such a simple conclusion. One does not simply NOT DO things because he thinks he can’t. An ordinary human being, being a social creature, considers a lot many more factors rather than the simple ignorant fact that he can’t do what he wants to. I couldn’t vouch enough for how wrong that statement is. Yeah, I have come across such phrases before - “Nothing is impossible”, “You can’t do it if you think you can’t”. And no, I haven’t questioned them before, because they were meant in a motivational context. But reading Allen’s work, where he analyses human mind, and spreads out reasons why we’re all doing it all wrong ‘mentally’, I had to say it. <br />And I don’t mean to be demotivating. If you are inspired by this work, that’s a good thing, go on with your life. But if you are anything like me, you might be criticizing the book too, and I’m merely contributing my opinions.<br /><br />	●<blockquote>
  <b>
    <i> “ALL that a man achieves and all that he fails to achieve is the direct result of his own thoughts”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br /><br />Please don’t get me started on this one again. A man simply doesn’t fail because he thought them all wrong. And a man wouldn’t conquer the world with his stupid domineering thoughts. <br /><br />	●<blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“To desire is to obtain; to aspire is to, achieve.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br />You get that? <b>It’s the same thing over and over again.</b> I’m amazed he managed to stretch it out for a full 65 pages. That’s impressive vocabulary skills. Blah.<br /><br />This one might be the truest thing he said, but it is not a fact at all. It doesn’t work in all situations. Like those physics theories we were forced to learn in high school? Applies to some places but doesn’t run true for the rest. <br />	<blockquote>
  <b>The strength of the effort is the measure of the result.</b>
</blockquote><br /><br />All in all, I get that while James Allen tried some old-school motivational lines, (okay, maybe he is the master of those ‘old-school’ motivational lines. This was published in what? 1902?), it didn’t work with me. That might be because I’m unmoved by non-fiction and motivational pieces in general, so you may still want to read this book. And yet, I say,<b> “A man is literally what he thinks, his character being the complete sum of all his thoughts.” - NOT.</b></span>
  <a data-text-id="8799674894196743018" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/23591855-viji-bookish-endeavors?shelf=non-fiction">non-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/23591855-viji-bookish-endeavors?shelf=self-help">self-help</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer873798549" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13828647064429212112"><i>Close your eyes.. <br/>look deep into yourself.. <br/>what do you see.?<br/>red..? black.?<br/>no.. go deeper..<br/>concentrate on your breath.. <br/>unable to concentrate..?<br/>finding some murmurs in the background.?<br/>well.. those are your thoughts.. <br/>those thoughts which fill your mind every moment..<br/>most of us do not observe our thoughts.<br/>start observing them.. <br/>try to concentrate on each and every thought as a single grain of sand..<br/>most of them will be repetitive..<br/>eliminate them..<br/>fill your mind with cheerful thoughts..<br/>replace eve</i></span>
  <span id="freeText13828647064429212112" style="display:none"><i>Close your eyes.. <br />look deep into yourself.. <br />what do you see.?<br />red..? black.?<br />no.. go deeper..<br />concentrate on your breath.. <br />unable to concentrate..?<br />finding some murmurs in the background.?<br />well.. those are your thoughts.. <br />those thoughts which fill your mind every moment..<br />most of us do not observe our thoughts.<br />start observing them.. <br />try to concentrate on each and every thought as a single grain of sand..<br />most of them will be repetitive..<br />eliminate them..<br />fill your mind with cheerful thoughts..<br />replace every negative thought with a positive one..<br />think about what you wish to be and work for it..<br />you will find your whole life changing..<br />and all you did was observe and slightly alter your thoughts..</i><br /><br />This book is about the value of thoughts,how they influence a man,or rather how they make a man. The text is divided into different chapters,each on how thought is related to various aspects of life, and gives a clear and brief explanation of how thoughts influence one's life. To summarize the text in its own words..<br /><br /><b>* Thought and character</b><br />“Of all the beautiful truths pertaining to the soul which have been restored and brought to light in this age, none is more gladdening or fruitful of divine promise and confidence than this—that man is the master of thought, the moulder of character, and the maker and shaper of condition, environment, and destiny.”<br /><br /><b>*Effect of thought on circumstances</b><br />“The outer world of circumstance shapes itself to the inner world of thought, and both pleasant and unpleasant external conditions are factors, which make for the ultimate good of the individual. As the reaper of his own harvest, man learns both by suffering and bliss.”<br /><br /><b>*Effect of thought on health and the body</b><br />“THE body is the servant of the mind. It obeys the operations of the mind, whether they be deliberately chosen or automatically expressed. At the bidding of unlawful thoughts the body sinks rapidly into disease and decay; at the command of glad and beautiful thoughts it becomes clothed with youthfulness and beauty.”<br /><br /><b>*Thought and purpose</b><br />“A man should conceive of a legitimate purpose in his heart, and set out to accomplish it. He should make this purpose the centralizing point of his thoughts. It may take the form of a spiritual ideal, or it may be a worldly object, according to his nature at the time being; but whichever it is, he should steadily focus his thought-forces upon the object, which he has set before him.”<br /><br /><b>*The thought-factor in achievement</b><br />“ALL that a man achieves and all that he fails to achieve is the direct result of his own thoughts...Before a man can achieve anything, even in worldly things, he must lift his thoughts above slavish animal indulgence.”<br /><br /><b>*Visions and ideals</b><br />“The Vision that you glorify in your mind, the Ideal that you enthrone in your heart—this you will build your life by, this you will become.”<br /><br /><b>*Serenity</b><br />“CALMNESS of mind is one of the beautiful jewels of wisdom. It is the result of long and patient effort in self-control. Its presence is an indication of ripened experience, and of a more than ordinary knowledge of the laws and operations of thought.”<br /><br />Being brief and clear in presentation,this book is an excellent work in the self-help genre and unlike many others in that genre,interesting till the end. <br /><br /><br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="13828647064429212112" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781442118911" href="/book/show/6512835-as-a-man-thinketh">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Everyone</span></div>

          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Norm by: </span>
      A stranger willing to help me when I needed help.
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7066916-norm-davis?shelf=non-fiction">non-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7066916-norm-davis?shelf=philosophy">philosophy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7066916-norm-davis?shelf=classic">classic</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer346116440" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10010258298329618230">The first “self help” book I ever read was Norman Vincent Peale's “The Power of Positive Thinking”. I was a troubled kid seriously trudging down the “wrong road”. Seeing this and evidently caring about it, a “stranger” jewelry salesman at a large department store offered me the book. Guess he thought the loss of the book would be better than the loss of ear rings from his department around Mother's Day. <br/><br/>Since reading that book I have read in the neighborhood of 500-1,000 of these type of books. </span>
  <span id="freeText10010258298329618230" style="display:none">The first “self help” book I ever read was Norman Vincent Peale's “The Power of Positive Thinking”. I was a troubled kid seriously trudging down the “wrong road”. Seeing this and evidently caring about it, a “stranger” jewelry salesman at a large department store offered me the book. Guess he thought the loss of the book would be better than the loss of ear rings from his department around Mother's Day. <br /><br />Since reading that book I have read in the neighborhood of 500-1,000 of these type of books. What has always struck me was that each new book I read said pretty much what the others said except it was explained a little differently. I used to wonder where it started. Where do these obviously successful books come from? Where is their birth place? I read older and older of these type books and came to believe that this type of book has its beginnings lost in the annals of history. But for modern purposes this little volume, and the date it was written (century ago) has probably been devoured by every self-help guru that has ever written a newer self help book this century. <br /><br />As a Man Thinketh is pretty much where every modern day self help guru goes to or comes from, except they say it in about 10-100 times as many words as James Allen did.<br /><br />If you're inclined to take an interest in self help and you are not sure which guru is getting it right in the almighty sea of self help books you'll do yourself a great service if you read the 7 essays in this short book first. Most the rest the offerings are based on this little volume.<br /><br />“The Secret”, “The Law of Attraction”, etc., etc., are all pitching you As a Man Thinketh which you can get free audio at Librovox and free epub at Project Gutenberg. <br /><br />Oh yeah... everything in the book is top secret and is never to be told to anyone because they may turn out to be someone like Walt Disney, or Dale Carnage, or any of those other dreamers, thinkers, and capitalist. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="10010258298329618230" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

Cherish your ideals. Cherish the music that stirs in your heart, the beauty that forms in your mind, the loveliness that drapes your purest thoughts, for out of them will grow all delightful conditions, all heavenly environment, of these, if you but remain true to them your world will at last be built.<br /> The soul attracts that which it secretly harbors, that which it loves, and also that which it fears. It reaches the height of its cherished aspirations. It falls to the level of its unchastened desires - and circumstances are the means by which the soul receives its own.<br /> Men are anxious to improve their circumstances, but are unwilling to improve themselves, they therefore remain bound.<br /> Every action and feeling is preceded by a thought.<br /> Right thinking begins with the words we say to ourselves.<br /> Circumstance does not make the man, it reveals him to himself.<br /> You cannot travel within and stand still without.<br /> As the physically weak man can make himself strong by careful and patient training, so the man of weak thoughts, can make them strong by exercising himself in right thinking.<br /></span>

  <span id="freeText1608314126116242147" style="display:none">"To desire is to obtain; to aspire is to achieve."<br /><br />"You will become as small as your controlling desire; as great as your dominant aspiration:"<br /><br />How the author had managed to deliver so many helpful lessons in so little number of pages seems most incredible. <div id="review_115790891" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/115790891" />
    <a title="Hans" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1142366-hans"><img alt="Hans" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1292037372p2/1142366.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/115790891?book_show_action=true">Aug 08, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Hans" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Hans" href="/user/show/1142366-hans">Hans</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1142366-hans?shelf=philosophy">philosophy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1142366-hans?shelf=inspirational">inspirational</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1142366-hans?shelf=spiritual-development">spiritual-development</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer115790891" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15276759600303210132">This book could be summoned up as "You are ultimately responsible for your life through your thoughts". James Allen's presents his ideas like a no-holds-bar-stop-making-excuses-for-your-life slap in the face. I definitely agree with his major points though at times his moralizing seems a bit antiquated the core concepts are pretty solid. This book made me think about excuses, complaining and justifications vs. sacrifice and hard work. What I find intriguing about it is that all of us have such p</span>
  <span id="freeText15276759600303210132" style="display:none">This book could be summoned up as "You are ultimately responsible for your life through your thoughts". James Allen's presents his ideas like a no-holds-bar-stop-making-excuses-for-your-life slap in the face. I definitely agree with his major points though at times his moralizing seems a bit antiquated the core concepts are pretty solid. This book made me think about excuses, complaining and justifications vs. sacrifice and hard work. What I find intriguing about it is that all of us have such powerful inherent potential and yet we cut ourselves down and undermine our own efforts with useless and defeatist thinking. The interesting question is why we are so susceptible to it. Why are we sometimes seemingly so eager to excuse ourselves? We want to be let off the hook, dodge blame or anything else that may let us get away with doing less than we are capable. In the end more than trying to convince other people with our excuses it seems that we are trying the hardest to convince ourselves, the one person who it is the hardest to lie to since we know we can and ought to do more and be more. It reminds me of those oft heard quotes about mankind being terrified of their own potential greatness and instead spends more of their time hiding from it. We are paradoxical beings full of contradictions that on the surface make little apparent sense but underneath ultimately define what it means to be human.</span>
  <a data-text-id="15276759600303210132" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_345793421" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/345793421" />
    <a title="Rakhi Dalal" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3655942-rakhi-dalal"><img alt="Rakhi Dalal" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1557596257p2/3655942.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/345793421?book_show_action=true">Jun 10, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Rakhi Dalal" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Rakhi Dalal" href="/user/show/3655942-rakhi-dalal">Rakhi Dalal</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer345793421" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8575743642732367907">In the foreword, the Author says that this work is intended as suggestive rather than explanatory. He conveys that, this is not an exhaustive treatise, but a result of his own meditation and experience in the direction. I couldn’t but agree more with him.<br/><br/>Through this short book, James has explained relation of our thoughts with our character, health and circumstances. He has also tried to maintain a relation of our thoughts with purpose and achievement in life. Though the book is written in a mo</span>
  <span id="freeText8575743642732367907" style="display:none">In the foreword, the Author says that this work is intended as suggestive rather than explanatory. He conveys that, this is not an exhaustive treatise, but a result of his own meditation and experience in the direction. I couldn’t but agree more with him.<br /><br />Through this short book, James has explained relation of our thoughts with our character, health and circumstances. He has also tried to maintain a relation of our thoughts with purpose and achievement in life. Though the book is written in a most simple manner and proved to be a source of inspiration for many; I did not find myself agreeing with everything that it had to say. I agree that thoughts are powerful and can to an extent lead the way life moves, but they do not always have a role to play. <br /> <br />E.g. while explaining the relation of thought and circumstances, Allen says <i>"The outer conditions of a person's life will always be found to be harmoniously related to his inner state...Men do not attract that which they want, but that which they are.”</i>...... But this could not always be so. What could be said of a person who is exposed to disastrous circumstances coming out of the blue, with absolutely no relation to his/her past, or to the way he thinks? And of the suffering he might endure for that?<br /><br />Still it is a worth read once.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="8575743642732367907" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1635517756" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1635517756" />
    <a title="Josh" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/37929896-josh"><img alt="Josh" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1423941056p2/37929896.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1635517756?book_show_action=true">May 11, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Josh" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Josh" href="/user/show/37929896-josh">Josh</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1635517756" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6128014168651087915">"ALL that a man achieves and all that he fails to achieve is the direct result of his own thoughts. In a justly ordered universe, where loss of equipoise would mean total destruction, individual responsibility must be absolute. A man's weakness and strength, purity and impurity, are his own, and not another man's; they are brought about by himself, and not by another; and they can only be altered by himself, never by another. His condition is also his own , and not another man's. His suffering a</span>
  <span id="freeText6128014168651087915" style="display:none">"ALL that a man achieves and all that he fails to achieve is the direct result of his own thoughts. In a justly ordered universe, where loss of equipoise would mean total destruction, individual responsibility must be absolute. A man's weakness and strength, purity and impurity, are his own, and not another man's; they are brought about by himself, and not by another; and they can only be altered by himself, never by another. His condition is also his own , and not another man's. His suffering and his happiness are evolved from within. As he thinks , so he is; as he continues to think, so he remains."<br /><br />Well that's really the majority of it in a nutshell, isn't it? This book, written in 1902, is about positive thought and its effect on your life's results. While I don't agree with the idea that someone's poor health or true tragedies are a result of pure negative thought, I do agree that one's thoughts and attitude have a great impact on their level of success/happiness.<br /><br />I also think that in a world where we attribute much of one's bad actions as someone else's fault, (mommy didn't love me enough so I commit crimes) we could use a little more of the idea that it may just be our own faults when we screw up.<br /><br />All-in-all a good, classic, one-time read.</span>
  <a data-text-id="6128014168651087915" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>
